Maintenance For Scripts En
Ultra-detailed maintenance and rebuild manual for the DedSec Project Python repository, produced from direct source inspection.

Scope
This document covers every Python file found in the repository, including the root-side English tree, the Greek mirror tree, and archived scripts under Extra Content/Unused Scripts. The goal is not only to explain what each script appears to do, but also to make future maintenance easier by identifying change points, execution style, code structure, data touchpoints, and minimum rebuild/test actions.

Safety boundary
Some folders contain deceptive-style pages or data-collection themed components. Those scripts are documented here at the level of code structure, maintenance, architecture, and refactor planning. This manual does not turn them into step-by-step misuse instructions.

Repository sculpture
- Total Python files inspected: 168
- Root-side or English/archived files: 94
- Greek mirror files: 74
- Parse-damaged files: 2
- Flask-style web files detected: 103
- Files with subprocess or shell execution signals: 159
- Files with explicit network-client signals: 57
- Category counts:
  - ButSystem.py: 2
  - Developer Base: 8
  - Extra Content.py: 2
  - Fake Pages: 25
  - Games: 5
  - Network Tools: 10
  - Other Tools: 6
  - Personal Information Capture: 17
  - Settings.py: 2
  - Unused Scripts: 20
  - Άλλα Εργαλεία: 6
  - Βάση Προγραμματιστή: 8
  - Εργαλεία Δικτύου: 10
  - Παιχνίδια: 5
  - Πλαστές Σελίδες: 25
  - Συλλογή Προσωπικών Πληροφοριών: 17

How to use this manual
- Read the repository-level guidance first.
- When changing a single script, use its per-file entry as a mini change map: where logic lives, where I/O happens, where routes or menus are defined, and what should be tested after edits.
- When changing mirrored features, update the English or root-side file first, test behavior, then port the same behavior to the Greek mirror while keeping translated UI text aligned.
- When doing larger cleanup, centralize paths, shell commands, HTTP settings, and user-facing strings before changing deeper logic.

Repository-wide maintainability strategy derived from the code
- Centralize absolute paths and storage folders. Many scripts assume fixed Termux-style locations and will break quietly when those assumptions drift.
- Separate UI/menu code from business logic. Many files are easiest to improve when prompts, actions, parsing, and persistence are moved into dedicated helpers.
- Separate transport from parsing. Any file that performs requests, scans, or route handling becomes easier to test when network transport and data interpretation live in different functions.
- Reduce giant top-level blocks. Large procedural flows should be moved into named steps so a future maintainer can change one stage without re-reading the entire file.
- Keep the Greek mirror behavior-locked to the English tree. Translations should mostly change visible strings, not core logic.
- For archived files, decide whether they are preserved for history only or should still be runnable. That choice should be written down, because inactive scripts decay fastest.

What to edit when requirements change
- route URLs
- form field names

- output folder constants

How to make this file easier to maintain
- move magic paths, ports, filenames, and URLs into a small config block at the top
- keep business logic in helpers and keep the entry/menu layer thin
- separate HTML/template text from request handling so route logic stays easier to test
- wrap shell calls in one helper that returns status, stdout, and stderr for easier debugging

Minimum rebuild checklist
- run the main menu once and verify every visible branch still opens
- smoke-test each route and every expected form key or upload path
- write to a temporary folder and verify created files and JSON shape
- test shell wrappers with both installed and missing dependency scenarios
